i &lt; squares.size(); i++)</p><p>    {</p><p>        cv::Rect rectangle = boundingRect(Mat(squares[i]));</p><p>        if ((rectangle.width &gt;= max_width) &amp;&amp; (rectangle.height &gt;= max_height))</p><p>        {</p><p>            max_width = rectangle.width;</p><p>            max_height = rectangle.height;</p><p>            max_square_idx = i;</p><p>        }</p><p>    }</p><p>    biggest_square = squares[max_square_idx];</p><p>    return max_square_idx;</p><p>}</p><p>//ä¸»å‡½æ•°ï¼Œå°ç¼–è¿™é‡Œåçœä¸€ä¸‹ï¼Œæ²¡æœ‰æŠŠä¸€äº›å‡½æ•°å°è£…èµ·æ¥ï¼Œæ˜¾å¾—æ¯”è¾ƒä¹±ï¼Œå°ç¼–å»ºè®®å¤§å®¶å…»æˆæŠŠå¤„ç†å¾—å‡½æ•°éƒ½å°è£…èµ·æ¥ï¼Œä¸»å‡½æ•°å°±ä¸ä¼šåƒå°ç¼–è¿™æ ·çœ‹ä¸Šå»å¾ˆä¹±äº†ã€‚</p><p>int main(int argc, char *argv[])</p><p>{</p><p>    Mat src,dst,gray,binarization,open,dilate_img,gauss_img,edges_img;</p><p>   src = imread(&#34;/home/shangbinbin/opencv_linux_test/test3/4.jpg&#34;);</p><p>//å¤„ç†ä¸ºç°åº¦å›¾</p><p>  cvtColor(src,gray,CV_BGR2GRAY);</p><p>//é«˜æ–¯æ»¤æ³¢</p><p>  GaussianBlur(gray,gauss_img,Size(3,3),2,2);</p><p>//è¾¹ç¼˜æ£€æµ‹</p><p>  Canny(gauss_img,edges_img,50,150,3);</p><p>//è†¨èƒ€</p><p>  dilate(edges_img, dilate_img, Mat(), cv::Point(-1, -1), 3, 1, 1);</p><p>//å®šä¹‰å®¹å™¨ç±»å‹å¾—å˜é‡ï¼Œä¸å¤ªæ˜ç™½å¾—å¯ä»¥çœ‹çœ‹C++çš„å®¹å™¨è¿™ä¸€éƒ¨åˆ†çŸ¥è¯†</p><p>  vector&lt;vector&lt;cv::Point&gt; j++)</p><p>                  {</p><p>                      double cosine = fabs(getAngle(approx[j%4], approx[j-2], approx[j-1]));</p><p>                      maxCosine = MAX(maxCosine, cosine);</p><p>                  }</p><p>                      //è§’åº¦å¤§æ¦‚72åº¦</p><p>                  if (maxCosine &lt; class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><b>èˆå¼—å‹’è‹±æ–‡é¢è¯•é—®æˆ‘çš„é—®é¢˜</b></p><p>1.ä½ çš„çˆ±å¥½æ˜¯ä»€ä¹ˆï¼Œä¸ºä»€ä¹ˆä½ å–œæ¬¢å®ƒ</p><p>2.å½“ä½ å‹åŠ›å¤§çš„æ—¶å€™ä½ ä¼šåšä»€ä¹ˆ</p><p>3.åœ¨ä¸€ä¸ªå›¢é˜Ÿä¸­ä½ å–œæ¬¢æ‹…ä»»ä»€ä¹ˆæ ·çš„èŒä½ï¼Œä¸ºä»€ä¹ˆï¼Ÿ</p><p><b>èˆå¼—å‹’ç¬”è¯•ï¼ˆé€‰æ‹©é¢˜ï¼‰</b></p><p><i>1.</i></p><p><i>You are in a project meeting where your immediate manager and the Department Head are discussing a certain aspect of the project. The situation and problems are complex and certain areas are even beyond your understanding but it looks like there are only 2 possible options at this point in time. It becomes clear to you that the two of them have very different and strong opinions about which decision and direction should be appropriate to take. Each has his own views, with a good mix of strong arguments for his decision, with identified limitations, risks and potential consequences. They have turned to you to ask you for your opinion and to choose which one you will support. What do you do?</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. Since both options have their own share of benefits and risk and limitations, it makes more sense for me to support my immediate manager since he will have more influence over my daily work and year-end appraisal. </i></p><p><i>B. The Department Head is obviously more senior in rank and experienced in such matters. It is also more appropriate to support him as he is the overall person in charge and will make the final decision anyway. </i></p><p><i>C.This is an awkward situation. They may have personal differences that I am not aware of and it is best for me not to take sides and get involved. I will declare that I am new and inexperienced and will defer to any decision made as I am sure it will be the best. </i></p><p><i>D. I consider all points of discussion, combine the best of both options and offer this as a better alternative which would be ideal for the situation. </i></p><p><i>E. I consider both options carefully and select one of them, with my own comments and reasons.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>2.</i></p><p><i>You work in a team of 5 with a supervisor and a manager managing your team and other teams in this department. In your first project within your team, in one of the internal discussions, you feel that some figures are interpreted and presented inaccurately although the primary data and facts are accurate. You raised your questions and concerns to the team leader, David. David is one of your co-workers who is the most senior in terms of years of service. He appears to have good relationships with everyone, especially with the supervisor. David listens to you but feels confident about the situation and thinks that the interpretation is not inaccurate and even if it is, the primary data and facts remain unchanged and are easily accessible by most people involved in the project. This is a team project and one of many that you will be involved in, mostly with members of your same team. What do you do?</i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCDE</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. I will just let the situation remain as it is since I have done my part in raising my concerns and questions and received his response. Afterall, David will be responsible for the project and should be able to respond to any questions asked. </i></p><p><i>B. Since David does not want to listen to me and make any changes, I feel that I will need to speak to my Department Head about this. It will be more appropriate for the Department Head to address this sensitive situation than for me to push on. </i></p><p><i>C. I raise my concern immediately with our supervisor and voiced my displeasure about how uncooperative David has been and how he appears so unconcerned about the quality of the data used and how this may affect the project&#39;s success. </i></p><p><i>D. I discussed with other team members to cross check my understanding of the situation and whether my assumptions and thinking are also shared. If there is a common understanding of the situation, I will again try to confront David, perhaps with other team members, to clarify the situation. </i></p><p><i>E. I call to arrange a meeting with David and our supervisor to confront the issue as I feel that it is important to clarify the situation and problem once and for all.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>3.</i></p><p><i>You are currently researching some material to support your team leader on a project involving the development of a new process. The project is of high importance and is closely watched by the CEO due to the potential benefits it could bring to the company. The deadline for submitting your research material is by tomorrow morning, the deadline cannot be delayed as it will affect other stages of the project. At noon, your supervisor asked you to read a set of presentation material which is required for tomorrow&#39;s breakfast meeting with some customers. Your role tomorrow will be to meet, greet and brief the customers and you will be supporting a discussion session. You have supported a similar event last year and played a similar role as well. However, you know that the research still requires more time and it is likely you may need your evening time as well to complete the task. What do you do? </i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCDE</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. The research work is clearly more important. I will explain my situation to my supervisor and politely request to be excused from the breakfast meeting as I am sure he will understand. </i></p><p><i>B. I will read the presentation material early tomorrow morning and continue with my research in order to complete my current task. </i></p><p><i>C. I will read the presentation material straight away and check with my supervisor for any guidance and confirm my role for tomorrow&#39;s breakfast meeting. Then, I will continue my research work. </i></p><p><i>D. I will continue my research and quickly complete and submit this somehow by 5pm. Then, I can read the presentation material for the breakfast meeting and complete this before I go off for the day. </i></p><p><i>E. I will place my research as a priority and only read the presentation material if I have time. I am confident of managing through the situation tomorrow morning as I am familiar with the event.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>4.</i></p><p><i>You have been asked to participate in a cross-functional team to work on a certain topical problem which is not your familiar area of knowledge. At the same time, you are asked to work on another project in your department. This project topic is more familiar as you have handled a similar project previously. You have complete freedom to choose either project, but you can only choose one. What do you do? </i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--AB</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. I will choose the project in the cross functional team and try my best and hope that I can be of help and learn as much as I can at the same time. </i></p><p><i>B. I feel that choosing a project not in my familiar area is risky and also will limit the contributions to the company in that project. I will therefore stick to the project in my department as I feel I can contribute more quickly and greatly to this area. This will also allow me to return to my regular role quickly.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>5.</i></p><p><i>You have just been promoted to handle a new small team whom you have not worked with before. You are aware that there are performance issues for a long time. Many of the team members are long-time staff in the company although not all have been in the same team together for that long. Your manager has asked you to fix the situation quickly because this is exactly you why you have been promoted. What is your preferred way of dealing with this situation?</i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABC</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. I quickly announced to the team that I have taken over as their leader, declare that poor performance issues will not be tolerated anymore and ask everyone to raise his/her level of performance from this day onwards. </i></p><p><i>B. I try to make friends with as many members of the team as possible and persuade them to improve their performance over time. It is more practical this way as this will ensure that I can manage the motivation level, retain everyone in the team and ensure a more sustainable improvement over time. </i></p><p><i>C. I take some time to understand the performance issues and process, in addition, I will get insight and feedback from people working within and outside the team. I then communicate to the team the situation and impact of the problems to other teams and the company. I share my plans and try to create an open environment where my team members can approach me with any questions.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>6.</i></p><p><i>You are writing a report to submit to your immediate manager for a project. A more experienced member of the team informs you that she thinks the report could be improved if you change the order and content of certain sections. What do you do?</i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCD</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. I quickly make the changes she suggested and thank her for being helpful. </i></p><p><i>B. I thank her for her comments and suggestions but decide that it is wiser to stick to my original work so that I can be proud of it. Even if I am not perfect, the work is truly mine and not helped by anyone. </i></p><p><i>C. I make selective changes to the report only where it matters. </i></p><p><i>D. I discuss with her to understand her reasons for the changes proposed before deciding whether and how much to change the report.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>7.</i></p><p><i>You are about to start your rotation in the Finance department as part of the training for new graduates. You will be joining the Finance department at the busiest period of the year when it is involved in annual business and budget planning. Your new supervisor briefly informed you 2 weeks before you are due to go over that you will be joining a special project team in Finance to support the development of a new process and tool supporting budget planning. You have not worked in any Finance role before. What do you do?</i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCD</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. I research the internet to find out everything about business planning an annual budgeting process. </i></p><p><i>B. I will speak to my current supervisor to request for early release and transfer to the Finance department so that I can have a headstart to the project and get to meet my new colleagues. </i></p><p><i>C. Thank the new supervisor and request her to email you more information about the project so that you can be more prepared. </i></p><p><i>D. Thank the new supervisor and inform her that you would like to meet up with her next week to find out more about the details of the project you will be involved in.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>8.</i></p><p><i>You have arranged to meet up with a colleague from another department in order to explain about the project you are leading and request for the information you need. Your colleague arrived on time and mention that she could only spare half an hour instead of one hour. During the meeting, your colleague appears distracted and in a rush. She apologised and hands you some pieces of paper stating that the information contained should be enough for you to get started. After the meeting, you reviewed the information thoroughly and feel that you do not have everything that you need for your project. What do you do?</i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCD</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. Call my colleague to clarify the information she provided and the need for more data. Get started with the areas of information I feel more confident about. </i></p><p><i>B. I know my colleague is busy and I will stick to the information given and make the best out of it. </i></p><p><i>C. Send an email to the colleague with all the questions I want the answers to. </i></p><p><i>D. Wait till my colleague has more time to spare before I approach her on the same topic.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>9.</i></p><p><i>You accompanied your Sales Manager to the site of Customer A to support a customer survey exercise. The survey interview is held in a meeting room. Just as you are about to complete your interview with Customer A, you received a call on silent mode, and you recognize that it is from Customer C. You guess that Customer C may want to discuss some things concerning the same survey you had earlier conducted as he had some questions the last time. What do you do next? </i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCD</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. Ask my Sales Manager to help me continue and conclude the survey so that I can take the call from Customer C immediately. </i></p><p><i>B. Excuse myself from the meeting room immediately to take the call from Customer C. </i></p><p><i>C. Pick up the call and inform Customer C that I would call him/her back later as I was in the middle of another meeting. </i></p><p><i>D. Do not pick up the call. Call Customer C back later.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>10.</i></p><p><i>You have just received a brief email from another manager, highlighting that you could have been more tactful and diplomatic in your response to a customer&#39;s challenge on some quality issues. You remember that the customer in the end accepted your data and explanation and you feel justified in your approach. your immediate manager, who was also present, did not comment further. What do you do? </i></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>--è¯·é€‰æ‹©--ABCD</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p><i>A. Reply to the other manager, thank him and explain politely and factually what happened and why I maintain that it was appropriate for me to do so. </i></p><p><i>B. Decide not to make an issue of it and let the email go unreplied since my immediate manager did not comment me on the same thing. </i></p><p><i>C. Call the other manager up immediately to find out more about his point of view. </i></p><p><i>D. Check with my immediate manager to get his feedback on the same situation before reaching out to the other manager to understand his comments.</i></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p class=\"ztext-empty-paragraph\"><br/></p><p>æ€»çš„æ¥è¯´ï¼Œè¿˜æ˜¯éå¸¸æ„Ÿè°¢è¿™ä¸¤æ®µå®ä¹ ç»å†ï¼Œè¿™ä¹Ÿæ˜¯æˆ‘èƒ½è·å¾—14ä¸ªofferçš„å¿…è¦æ¡ä»¶ä¹‹ä¸€å§ã€‚å°±ç®—æ²¡æ—¶é—´å®ä¹ ï¼Œå¯¼å¸ˆä¸æ”¾äººï¼Œä¹Ÿå¯ä»¥å»é¢è¯•ä¸€ä¸‹å®ä¹ ï¼Œæé«˜è‡ªå·±çš„é¢è¯•èƒ½åŠ›ï¼Œçœçš„ç­‰ç§‹æ‹›åˆ°äº†æœ‰ç‚¹æªä¸åŠæ‰‹ã€‚</p><p></p>",
